###### ‡∏à‡∏±‡∏î‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏î‡∏π‡πÅ‡∏•‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢ [‡∏Ñ‡∏ì‡∏∞‡∏Å‡∏£‡∏£‡∏°‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏≥‡∏ô‡∏ß‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£](#steering-committee) ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ [‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡∏£‡πà‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô](#collaborators)

# Best Practices ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ ‡∏Ç‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ß‡∏•‡πà‡∏≤‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î

- **üîñ ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏ô‡∏π‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÅ‡∏ó‡πá‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà**: ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏ô‡∏π‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏û‡∏ß‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏î‡∏õ‡∏∏‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏õ‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏õ‡∏¥‡∏î‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á `#tags`. ‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡∏ä‡∏°‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á `#strategic` ‡∏Å‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ. ‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡∏ä‡∏°‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÅ‡∏ß‡∏∞‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏î‡∏π‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡πÇ‡∏ü‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏™‡∏´‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà `#new`. ‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏ä‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏ä‡∏≤‡∏ç‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏Å‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏´‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà `#advanced` ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ. ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≠‡∏ô‡∏∏‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏∞‡∏´‡πå‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì [Rubek Joshi](https://github.com/rubek-joshi@rubek-joshi)


- **üë®‚Äçüë©‚Äçüëß‚Äçüë¶ ‡∏™‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏ä‡∏¥‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏ö‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ß!**: ‡∏°‡∏µ repository ‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏ö‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏≤ - [‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥ Best Practices ‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ Integration Tests ‡∏ö‡∏ô Node.js ‚ú®](https://github.com/testjavascript/nodejs-integration-tests-best-practices). ‡∏ã‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡∏°‡∏µ best practices ‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ 40 ‡∏´‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ô component tests ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏ó‡∏û‡∏ã‡πà‡∏≤‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏¥‡∏ó‡∏ò‡∏¥‡∏†‡∏≤‡∏û‡∏ö‡∏ô Node.js

# ‡∏¢‡∏¥‡∏ô‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏ô‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö! ‡∏°‡∏µ 3 ‡∏™‡∏¥‡πà‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏£‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏£‡∏π‡πâ‡∏Å‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ô‡∏ô

**1. ‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏Å‡∏≥‡∏•‡∏±‡∏á‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏ö‡∏ó‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î ‡∏à‡∏≥‡∏ô‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö Node.js -** repository ‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏™‡∏£‡∏∏‡∏õ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏î‡∏π‡πÅ‡∏•‡πÄ‡∏ô‡∏∑‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏ó‡πá‡∏≠‡∏õ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á Node.js best practices, ‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏ô‡∏∑‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ô‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡∏ó‡∏µ‡∏°‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô

**2. ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏ö‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏¢‡∏≠‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î, ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏±‡∏û‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏ó‡∏ó‡∏∏‡∏Å‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏¥‡∏ï‡∏¢‡πå -** ‡∏Ç‡∏ì‡∏∞‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πâ‡∏°‡∏µ‡πÄ‡∏ô‡∏∑‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ô‡∏≥‡πÄ‡∏™‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö best practices, style guides, ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏•‡πá‡∏î‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏™‡∏ñ‡∏≤‡∏õ‡∏±‡∏ï‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏£‡∏£‡∏° ‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ 80 ‡∏ö‡∏ó‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°. Issues and pull requests ‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏™‡∏£‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏∏‡∏Å‡∏ß‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏´‡∏ô‡∏±‡∏á‡∏™‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏•‡πà‡∏°‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡∏¢‡∏π‡πà‡πÄ‡∏™‡∏°‡∏≠.‡∏¥‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏≠‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏£‡πà‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏≠‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢ ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÅ‡∏Å‡πâ code ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ú‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏û‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏î, ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ß‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÅ‡∏õ‡∏•‡∏†‡∏≤‡∏©‡∏≤ ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ ‡πÄ‡∏™‡∏ô‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏¢‡πÄ‡∏à‡πã‡∏á‡πÜ‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡πÜ, ‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô [Guideline ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πà](./.operations/writing-guidelines.md)

**3. # `1. ‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á Project Structure`

## ![‚úî] 1.1 ‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á Structure ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏≠‡∏¥‡∏á components ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏´‡∏•‡∏±‡∏Å

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏û‡∏±‡∏í‡∏ô‡∏≤ App ‡∏Ç‡∏ô‡∏≤‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏ç‡πà‡∏°‡∏±‡∏Å‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏´‡∏•‡∏∏‡∏°‡∏û‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏ç‡πà‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î‡∏ô‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Ñ‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ Maintain codebase ‡∏Ç‡∏ô‡∏≤‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏ç‡πà‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ dependency ‡∏ô‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏£‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢ - ‡∏ã‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏´‡∏•‡πà‡∏≤ dev ‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏´‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏¢‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö feature ‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡πÜ. ‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏≤‡πÅ‡∏ö‡πà‡∏á code ‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô component ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏≠‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡∏π‡πà‡πÉ‡∏ô folder ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ dedicated codebase, ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏ä‡∏¥‡πâ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏•‡πá‡∏Å ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ ‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏à‡∏á‡πà‡∏≤‡∏¢. ‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏õ '‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°' ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏•‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏î‡∏π‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á Project Structure ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠ developer ‡∏û‡∏±‡∏í‡∏ô‡∏≤ feature ‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏≤ ‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ impact ‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ code ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏ó‡∏≥ component ‡∏≠‡∏∑‡πà‡∏ô‡∏ö‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏°‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏õ‡∏•‡πà‡∏≤ - ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ deploy ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏•‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏™‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏á‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏¥‡∏° ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ scale ‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏¥‡∏° ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏¢‡∏Å business unit ‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á Structure ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏≠‡∏¥‡∏á components ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏´‡∏•‡∏±‡∏Å**](./sections/projectstructre/breakintcomponents.md)

## ![‚úî] 1.2 ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á Layer ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á component ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÜ, ‡∏™‡∏£‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡∏ï‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö web layer

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏•‡∏∞ component ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏£‡∏°‡∏µ 'layers' - ‡∏ã‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô object ‡πÑ‡∏ß‡πâ‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏ß‡πá‡∏ö, ‡∏•‡∏≠‡∏à‡∏¥‡∏Ñ, ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ code ‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏π‡∏• ‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏î‡∏π‡∏™‡∏∞‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏î‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥ separation of concerns ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏î‡∏µ ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥ mock ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ test ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏á‡πà‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢ ‡πÅ‡∏°‡πâ‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πà‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô pattern ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡πÄ‡∏´‡πá‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ó‡∏±‡πà‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡∏û‡∏±‡∏í‡∏ô‡∏≤ API ‡∏°‡∏±‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏° layers ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏™‡πà‡∏á web layer objects (‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô req, res ‡πÉ‡∏ô Express ) ‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏´‡∏≤ business logic ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ layer ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏π‡∏• - ‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πà‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ application ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏û‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡∏û‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ web frameworks ‡∏ö‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** App ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏° web objects ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö layer ‡∏≠‡∏∑‡πà‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ code ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ test ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ, CRON jobs, ‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å triggers ‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å message queues ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏ô

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á Layer ‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ app**](./sections/projectstructre/createlayers.md)

## ![‚úî] 1.3 ‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏ö utilities ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏ö‡πà‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô npm packages

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡πÉ‡∏ô app ‡∏Ç‡∏ô‡∏≤‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏ç‡πà‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ codebase ‡∏Ç‡∏ô‡∏≤‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏ç‡πà, ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ cross-cutting-concern utilities ‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô logger, ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏´‡∏±‡∏™‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏≠‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏ó‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡πÜ‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô, ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å wrap ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢ code ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡∏¥‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏ú‡∏¢‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏ê‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏∞ npm packages ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß. ‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πà‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÅ‡∏ö‡πà‡∏á‡∏õ‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ô‡∏≥‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÜ‡πÉ‡∏ô codebases ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ projects

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏Ñ‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ deploy ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ dependency wheel ‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡∏ã‡∏∞

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á Structure ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏´‡∏•‡∏±‡∏Å feature**](./sections/projectstructre/wraputilities.md)

## ![‚úî] 1.4 ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡πà‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏¢‡∏Å Express 'app' ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö 'server' ‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡πÄ‡∏•‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏á‡∏ô‡∏¥‡∏™‡∏±‡∏¢‡πÅ‡∏¢‡πà‡πÜ ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ [Express](https://expressjs.com/) app ‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏´‡∏°‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏ü‡∏•‡πå‡πÉ‡∏´‡∏ç‡πà‡πÑ‡∏ü‡∏•‡πå‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ß - ‡πÅ‡∏¢‡∏Å 'Express' ‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ô‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏™‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏ü‡∏•‡πå : ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏® API (app.js) ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ ‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥ networking (WWW). ‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏á structure ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏î‡∏µ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏® API ‡πÑ‡∏ß‡πâ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÉ‡∏ô components

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** API ‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å test ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏ú‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô HTTP ‡πÄ‡∏ó‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô (‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ ‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÜ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏ö‡∏Ñ‡∏•‡∏∏‡∏°‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ test). ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏Å‡πá‡∏Ñ‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏™‡∏ô‡∏∏‡∏Å‡πÅ‡∏ô‡πà‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏±‡πà‡∏á maintain code ‡∏´‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏£‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡∏ö‡∏£‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏±‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏ü‡∏•‡πå‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ß

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡πÅ‡∏¢‡∏Å Express 'app' ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö 'server'**](./sections/projectstructre/separateexpress.md)

## ![‚úî] 1.5 ‡∏Ñ‡∏≥‡∏ô‡∏∂‡∏á‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ï‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πà‡∏≤ environment, ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏õ‡∏•‡∏≠‡∏î‡∏†‡∏±‡∏¢ ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ hierarchy

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ï‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏≠‡∏£‡πå‡πÄ‡∏ü‡∏Ñ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏£‡πâ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏£‡∏Ñ‡∏≥‡∏ô‡∏∂‡∏á‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ (a) keys ‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÑ‡∏ü‡∏•‡πå file ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å environment variable (b) secrets ‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏Å‡πá‡∏ö‡πÅ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å code ‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà commit (c) ‡∏ï‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πà‡∏≤‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏•‡∏≥‡∏î‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏ä‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏™‡∏∞‡∏î‡∏ß‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏´‡∏≤ ‡∏°‡∏µ‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ö‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ"‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ö"‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏ö‡∏ï‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ö‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏Å‡πà. [rc](https://www.npmjs.com/package/rc), [nconf](https://www.npmjs.com/package/nconf), [config](https://www.npmjs.com/package/config), and [convict](https://www.npmjs.com/package/convict).

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏ï‡∏≤‡∏° requirements ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ö‡∏ô‡∏ã‡∏±‡∏Å‡∏≠‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡∏° dev ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ DevOps ‡∏ä‡∏∞‡∏á‡∏±‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏≠‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá‡∏ä‡∏∞‡∏á‡∏±‡∏Å‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏π‡πà

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ï‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πà‡∏≤‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö best practices**](./sections/projectstructre/configguide.md)

# `2. ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö Error`

## ![‚úî] 2.1 ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ Async-Await ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ promise ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÅ‡∏Å‡πâ async error

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö async errors ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ callback ‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏£‡πá‡∏ß‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ï‡∏Å‡∏ô‡∏£‡∏Å‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô (‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ ‡πÑ‡∏≠‡πâ‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏ß‡∏õ‡∏¥‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏¥‡∏î‡πÅ‡∏´‡πà‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏ä‡∏¥‡∏ö‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏¢) ‡∏™‡∏¥‡πà‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏°‡∏≠‡∏ö‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏Ñ‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô promise library ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÇ‡∏î‡πà‡∏á‡∏î‡∏±‡∏á ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ ‡∏ã‡∏∏‡∏õ‡∏ï‡∏≤‡∏£‡πå async-await ‡πÅ‡∏ó‡∏ô‡∏ã‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏î‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏ä‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏´‡∏ô‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏ï‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö syntax ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏û‡∏ß‡∏Å try-catch

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡∏™‡πÑ‡∏ï‡∏•‡πå callback ‡πÉ‡∏ô Node.js , ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô(err, response), ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ maintain ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠ error ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏õ‡∏Å‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏≠‡∏∑‡πà‡∏ô‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ã‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏∏‡∏Å‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡∏ï‡∏£‡∏¢‡∏∏‡πà‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏´‡∏¢‡∏¥‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î pattern ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏û‡∏¥‡∏®‡∏î‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ callback**](./sections/errorhandling/asyncerrorhandling.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 2.2 ‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà built-in Error object

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡∏´‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏Ñ‡∏ô throw error ‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô string ‡∏ö‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡πá‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô custom type ‡∏ö‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏•‡πà‡∏∞ ‚Äì ‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¥‡∏ò‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö error ‡∏î‡∏π‡∏¢‡∏∏‡πà‡∏á‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏ß‡∏∏‡πà‡∏ô‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏£  ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ ‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏£‡πà‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏´‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á modules. ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞ reject promise ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ throw exception ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏à‡∏∞ emit error ‚Äì ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà built-in Error object (‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ object ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏™‡∏£‡∏¥‡∏°‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö built-in Error object) ‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏™‡∏°‡πà‡∏≥‡πÄ‡∏™‡∏°‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏´‡∏ô‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ß‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏õ‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏π‡∏•‡∏™‡∏π‡∏ç‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏´‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏≠‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢. ‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏°‡∏µ `no-throw-literal` ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏é‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á ESLint ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ï‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏à‡∏™‡∏≠‡∏ö‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏°‡∏á‡∏ß‡∏î  (‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ [‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏à‡∏≥‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏î](https://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-throw-literal) ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡πÅ‡∏Å‡πâ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ TypeScript ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏ï‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πà‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏é `@typescript-eslint/no-throw-literal`)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ component ‡∏ö‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß, ‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏ä‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏£‡πå‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ errors ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡πÑ‡∏´‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏≤ ‚Äì ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö error ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏´‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏°‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏¢‡∏¥‡πà‡∏á‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÅ‡∏¢‡πà‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ custom types ‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏ò‡∏¥‡∏ö‡∏≤‡∏¢ errors ‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏π‡∏• error ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏Ñ‡∏±‡∏ç‡∏™‡∏π‡∏ç‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏¢‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô stack trace ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏ô!

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ built-in error object**](./sections/errorhandling/useonlythebuiltinerror.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.3 ‡∏à‡∏≥‡πÅ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏´‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á operational ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö programmer errors

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Operational errors (‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô API ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏π‡∏•‡∏ú‡∏¥‡∏î‡πÜ‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤) ‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏≠‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏≠‡∏¥‡∏á‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å Case ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÜ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏£‡∏π‡πâ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ú‡∏•‡∏Å‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏ö‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å Error ‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡πÜ‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏á ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô Programmer error (‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô ‡∏û‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡πÅ‡∏õ‡∏£ undefined) ‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏£‡∏π‡πâ‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ Code ‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏´‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏à‡πä‡∏á ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á Gracefully restart application

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏Å‡πá‡πÅ‡∏Ñ‡πà‡∏£‡∏µ‡πÅ‡∏≠‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏ó‡∏∏‡∏Å‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏à‡∏≠ Error ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÑ‡∏°‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏•‡∏ô‡πå 5,000 ‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏Ñ‡∏ô‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏´‡∏•‡∏∏‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏∞ Error ‡πÄ‡∏•‡πá‡∏Å‡πÜ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏Ñ‡∏≤‡∏î‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ì‡πå‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á operational error ‡∏≠‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏ï‡∏£‡∏á‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏•‡∏¢‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÅ‡∏≠‡∏õ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πÜ‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏°‡πâ‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏£‡∏π‡πâ‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏õ‡∏±‡∏ç‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏≠‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏£‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏£‡∏π‡πâ‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô (programmer error) ‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏´‡∏ï‡∏∏‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ì‡πå‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏≤‡∏î‡∏Ñ‡∏¥‡∏î‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ ‡∏à‡∏≥‡πÅ‡∏ô‡∏Å Error ‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏™‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏î‡∏µ ‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏õ‡∏±‡∏ç‡∏´‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏ô‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏ô‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ô‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏°‡∏î‡∏∏‡∏•‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏Å‡πá‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏¢‡∏π‡πà‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏£‡∏¥‡∏ö‡∏ó‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: operational vs programmer error**](./sections/errorhandling/operationalvsprogrammererror.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.4 ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å Error ‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏á, ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÉ‡∏ô middleware

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Logic ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥ Error handling ‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô‡∏™‡πà‡∏á‡∏à‡∏î‡∏´‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏≠‡∏î‡∏°‡∏¥‡∏ô ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ logging ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å encapsulate ‡πÉ‡∏ô object ‡πÄ‡∏â‡∏û‡∏≤‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ endpoint ‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏´‡∏°‡∏î (‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô Express middleware, cron jobs, unit-testing) ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏ß‡∏•‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î Error

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠ Error ‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÜ‡πÄ‡∏î‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏ã‡πâ‡∏≥‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏ó‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏£ ‡∏ô‡∏∞‡∏à‡πä‡∏∞ 

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö Error ‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏á**](./sections/errorhandling/centralizedhandling.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.5 ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÄ‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏£ API errors ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ Swagger ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ GraphQL

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏Ñ‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ API ‡∏£‡∏π‡πâ‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ Errors ‡πÑ‡∏´‡∏ô‡∏ö‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏™‡πà‡∏á‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏û‡∏ß‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏ö‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏°. ‡∏™‡∏≥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö RESTful API ‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏´‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏¢, ‡∏õ‡∏Å‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ documentation frameworks ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô Swagger. ‡∏ñ‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ GraphQL, ‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ schema ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ comments ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡∏Ñ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ API ‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏Ñ‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏°‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏£‡∏µ‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ Error ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏à‡∏Å‡∏•‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏≤ Note: ‡∏ã‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å API ‡∏Å‡πá‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏ô‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡πÅ‡∏´‡∏•‡∏∞ (‡∏õ‡∏Å‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ô‡πÇ‡∏•‡∏Å‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á microservice)

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏ó‡∏≥ Document API errors ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ Swagger ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ GraphQL**](./sections/errorhandling/documentingusingswagger.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.6 ‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å process ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö graceful ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏™‡∏¥‡πà‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏õ‡∏•‡∏Å‡∏õ‡∏•‡∏≠‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏¢‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ô

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡∏ï‡∏≠‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î Error ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏£‡∏π‡πâ‡∏à‡∏±‡∏Å (‡∏ñ‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô Developer error, ‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô best practice 2.3) - ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÉ‡∏à‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏Ç‡∏†‡∏≤‡∏û‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏≠‡∏õ‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏õ‡∏Å‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ Restart process ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏±‡∏î‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏ß‡∏±‡∏á ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏à‡∏±‡∏î‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ process ‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô [Forever](https://www.npmjs.com/package/forever) ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ [PM2](http://pm2.keymetrics.io/)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏µ exception ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏ï‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô, object ‡∏ö‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏≠‡∏¢‡∏π‡πà‡πÉ‡∏ô faulty state (‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô event emitter ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö global ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏™‡πà‡∏á events ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≠‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏ú‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏û‡∏•‡∏≤‡∏î‡∏ö‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÉ‡∏ô) ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ requests ‡∏ó‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡∏´‡∏°‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏ô‡∏≤‡∏Ñ‡∏ï‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏ö‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏°‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡πÅ‡∏õ‡∏•‡∏Å‡πÜ

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏õ‡∏¥‡∏î process**](./sections/errorhandling/shuttingtheprocess.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.7 ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠ Log ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà mature ‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏ä‡∏±‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏à‡∏ô‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á error

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡πÑ‡∏≠‡πâ‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏ß‡∏û‡∏ß‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠ logging ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÜ‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô [Pino](https://github.com/pinojs/pino) ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ [Log4js](https://www.npmjs.com/package/log4js), ‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏´‡∏≤ error ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏à‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÑ‡∏ß‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô ‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏£‡∏≤‡∏∞‡∏á‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡πá‡∏•‡∏∑‡∏° console.log ‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏•‡∏¢

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡∏Å‡πá‡∏´‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏î‡∏¥‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å console.logs ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ text file ‡∏£‡∏Å‡πÜ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì ‡∏ñ‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ querying tools ‡∏î‡∏µ‡πÜ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ log viewer ‡∏î‡∏µ‡πÜ‡∏ô‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏à‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏à‡∏≠‡∏à‡∏ô‡∏î‡∏∂‡∏Å‡∏Å‡πá‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏∞

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ mature logger**](./sections/errorhandling/usematurelogger.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.8 ‡∏ó‡∏î‡∏™‡∏≠‡∏ö flow ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á error ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ test framework ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏ä‡∏≠‡∏ö

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô Automated QA ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏î‡∏±‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏ó‡∏û‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Ñ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏ó‡∏™‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ò‡∏£‡∏£‡∏°‡∏î‡∏≤ ‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏°‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡πÉ‡∏à‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏î‡∏µ ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ return error ‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ Testing frameworks ‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô Mocha ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ Chai ‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏û‡∏ß‡∏Å‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πâ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏á‡πà‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏î‡∏≤‡∏¢ (‡∏î‡∏π‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏ï‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏ô "Gist popup")

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏ó‡∏™‡∏≠‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏≠, ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö auto ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ ‡πÄ‡∏ó‡∏™‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠, ‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡∏û‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡∏û‡∏≤‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ return errors ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ ‡∏ñ‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ error ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏´‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏¢ = ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö error ‡∏ô‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏≠‡∏á

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: testing error flows**](./sections/errorhandling/testingerrorflows.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.9 ‡∏´‡∏≤ errors ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ downtime ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ APM

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Monitoring and performance products (‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ APM) ‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏¥‡∏ô‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏†‡∏≤‡∏û Codebase ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠ API ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÉ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏ä‡∏¥‡∏á‡∏£‡∏∏‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ highlight errors, crashes, ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏à‡∏∏‡∏î‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏´‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÄ‡∏à‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏≠‡∏±‡∏ï‡πÇ‡∏ô‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ï‡∏¥

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏Å‡πá‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏£‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏¢‡∏≠‡∏∞‡πÜ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏ô‡∏±‡πà‡∏á‡∏ß‡∏±‡∏î‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏¥‡∏ó‡∏ò‡∏¥‡∏†‡∏≤‡∏û API ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö Downtimes ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏Ñ‡∏á‡∏´‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÄ‡∏à‡∏≠‡∏´‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏´‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏à‡∏£‡∏¥‡∏á ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏Å‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏ö‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≠‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏™‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ì‡πå‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏£‡∏ö‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏á

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏ú‡∏•‡∏¥‡∏ï‡∏†‡∏±‡∏ì‡∏ë‡πå APM **](./sections/errorhandling/apmproducts.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.10 Catch ‡∏™‡∏¥‡πà‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ handle ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á promise rejections

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Exception ‡πÉ‡∏î‡πÜ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å throw ‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å Promise ‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏ó‡∏¥‡πâ‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å ‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡∏û‡∏±‡∏í‡∏ô‡∏≤‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏•‡∏∑‡∏°‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏ä‡∏±‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏à‡∏ô ‡∏ñ‡∏∂‡∏á‡πÅ‡∏°‡πâ‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏à‡∏∞ subscribe ‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö `process.uncaughtException`! ‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ô‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£ register event `process.unhandledRejection`

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Errors ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏ö‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÑ‡∏£‡πâ‡∏£‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏≠‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ô‡πà‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏´‡πà‡∏ß‡∏á‡∏´‡∏£‡∏≠‡∏Å...‡∏°‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á?

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Catch ‡∏™‡∏¥‡πà‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ handle ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á promise rejections**](./sections/errorhandling/catchunhandledpromiserejection.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.11 Fail fast, ‡∏ï‡∏£‡∏ß‡∏à‡∏™‡∏≠‡∏ö arguments ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ library ‡πÄ‡∏â‡∏û‡∏≤‡∏∞‡∏ó‡∏≤‡∏á

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Assert API input ‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏•‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏á‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ô‡πà‡∏≤‡∏õ‡∏ß‡∏î‡∏´‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏Ç‡∏∂‡πâ‡∏ô‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏†‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏´‡∏•‡∏±‡∏á ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥ validation ‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ Code ‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏õ‡∏Å‡∏ï‡∏¥‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ô‡πà‡∏≤‡πÄ‡∏ö‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏ß‡πâ‡∏ô‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ helper library ‡∏™‡∏∏‡∏î‡∏Ñ‡∏π‡∏•‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô [ajv](https://www.npmjs.com/package/ajv) and [Joi](https://www.npmjs.com/package/joi)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡∏Ñ‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏á‡∏µ‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏∞‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏Ñ‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏∞‡∏°‡∏µ argument ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏•‡∏Ç‡∏ä‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠ ‚Äú‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏•‡∏î‚Äù ‡πÇ‡∏¢‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤ ‡πÅ‡∏ï‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏£‡∏µ‡∏¢‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏•‡∏∑‡∏°‡πÉ‡∏™‡πà‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏≤‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πá‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ Discount!=0 (‡∏à‡∏≥‡∏ô‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏•‡∏î‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤ 0) ‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡∏ú‡∏π‡πâ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏î‡∏™‡πà‡∏ß‡∏ô‡∏•‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏•‡πà‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏™‡∏ô‡∏∏‡∏Å‡∏™‡∏ô‡∏≤‡∏ô. ‡πÇ‡∏≠‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏´‡∏°‡πà‡∏≤‡∏¢‡∏Å‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏ô‡πà‡∏≤‡∏õ‡∏ß‡∏î‡∏´‡∏±‡∏ß‡∏à‡∏£‡∏¥‡∏á‡πÜ ‡πÄ‡∏´‡πá‡∏ô‡∏£‡∏∂‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á?

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: failing fast**](./sections/errorhandling/failfast.md)

## ![‚úî] 2.12 ‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á await promises ‡∏Å‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ô return ‡∏ó‡∏∏‡∏Å‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡πÄ‡∏•‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏á partial stacktrace

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** ‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á `return await` ‡∏ó‡∏∏‡∏Å‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏±‡πâ‡∏á‡πÄ‡∏°‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠ return promise ‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ error stacktrace ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏ï‡πá‡∏°‡πÜ. ‡∏ñ‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô returns promise ‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏ñ‡∏π‡∏Å‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏∞‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏®‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö `async` ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ `await` promise ‡∏Å‡πà‡∏≠‡∏ô return

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà return promise ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà await ‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡πÇ‡∏ú‡∏•‡πà‡∏ö‡∏ô stacktrace.
‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏°‡∏π‡∏•‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏¢‡πÑ‡∏õ‡∏≠‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏ó‡∏≥‡πÉ‡∏´‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏¢‡∏∏‡πà‡∏á‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏Å‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏Ç‡πâ‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏à‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏´‡∏≤ error ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÄ‡∏â‡∏û‡∏≤‡∏∞‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏¢‡∏¥‡πà‡∏á‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏ï‡πâ‡∏ô‡∏ï‡∏≠‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏õ‡∏±‡∏ç‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏µ‡πâ‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏¢‡πÑ‡∏õ

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: returning promises**](./sections/errorhandling/returningpromises.md)

# `3. Code Style Practices`

## ![‚úî] 3.1 ‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ ESLint

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** [ESLint](https://eslint.org) ‡∏ô‡∏±‡πâ‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏ï‡∏£‡∏ê‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πá‡∏Ñ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î error ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏õ‡∏£‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏™‡πÑ‡∏ï‡∏•‡πå‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏ô‡∏≠‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÅ‡∏Å‡πâ‡πÑ‡∏Ç‡∏õ‡∏±‡∏ç‡∏´‡∏≤ spacing ‡πÇ‡∏á‡πà‡πÜ‡πÅ‡∏•‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ß‡∏¢‡∏´‡∏≤‡πÇ‡∏Ñ‡πâ‡∏î‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏≥ anti-patterns ‡πÅ‡∏ö‡∏ö‡πÄ‡∏•‡∏ß‡∏£‡πâ‡∏≤‡∏¢‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô developer throw error ‡πÇ‡∏î‡∏¢‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏°‡∏µ classification. ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢ ESLint ‡∏Ñ‡∏∏‡∏ì‡∏™‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏£‡∏ñ‡πÅ‡∏Å‡πâ‡πÑ‡∏Ç code style ‡πÑ‡∏î‡πâ‡∏≠‡∏¢‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡∏≠‡∏±‡∏ï‡πÇ‡∏ô‡∏°‡∏±‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏£‡∏∑‡πà‡∏≠‡∏á‡∏°‡∏∑‡∏≠‡∏≠‡∏∑‡πà‡∏ô ‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô [prettier](https://www.npmjs.com/package/prettier) ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ [beautify](https://www.npmjs.com/package/js-beautify) ‡∏ã‡∏∂‡πà‡∏á‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÄ‡∏ó‡∏û‡∏Å‡∏ß‡πà‡∏≤‡πÉ‡∏ô‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÅ‡∏Å‡πâ‡πÑ‡∏Ç‡∏ï‡πà‡∏≤‡∏á‡πÜ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏¢‡∏±‡∏á‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô‡∏£‡πà‡∏ß‡∏°‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö ESLint ‡∏≠‡∏µ‡∏Å‡∏î‡πâ‡∏ß‡∏¢

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Developers ‡∏à‡∏∞‡πÇ‡∏ü‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏™‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏Ñ‡∏≤‡∏∞ space ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ ‡∏Ñ‡∏ß‡∏≤‡∏°‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡∏ö‡∏£‡∏£‡∏ó‡∏±‡∏î‡πÄ‡∏õ‡πá‡∏ô‡∏õ‡∏±‡∏ç‡∏´‡∏≤‡∏ó‡∏µ‡πà‡πÄ‡∏™‡∏µ‡∏¢‡πÄ‡∏ß‡∏•‡∏≤‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞‡∏Ñ‡∏¥‡∏î‡∏°‡∏≤‡∏Å‡∏à‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏¥‡∏î‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÄ‡∏Å‡∏µ‡πà‡∏¢‡∏ß‡∏Å‡∏±‡∏ö code style ‡∏Ç‡∏≠‡∏á‡πÇ‡∏õ‡∏£‡πÄ‡∏à‡∏Ñ

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: ‡∏Å‡∏≤‡∏£‡πÉ‡∏ä‡πâ‡∏á‡∏≤‡∏ô ESLint ‡πÅ‡∏•‡∏∞ Prettier**](./sections/codestylepractices/eslint_prettier.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.2 Node.js specific plugins

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** On top of ESLint standard rules that cover vanilla JavaScript, add Node.js specific plugins like [eslint-plugin-node](https://www.npmjs.com/package/eslint-plugin-node), [eslint-plugin-mocha](https://www.npmjs.com/package/eslint-plugin-mocha) and [eslint-plugin-node-security](https://www.npmjs.com/package/eslint-plugin-security)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Many faulty Node.js code patterns might escape under the radar. For example, developers might require(variableAsPath) files with a variable given as a path which allows attackers to execute any JS script. Node.js linters can detect such patterns and complain early

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.3 Start a Codeblock's Curly Braces on the Same Line

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** The opening curly braces of a code block should be on the same line as the opening statement

### Code Example

```javascript
// Do
function some‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô() {
  // code block
}

// Avoid
function some‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô() 
{
  // code block
}
```

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Deferring from this best practice might lead to unexpected results, as seen in the StackOverflow thread below:

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°:** "Why do results vary based on curly brace placement?" (StackOverflow)](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/3641519/why-does-a-results-vary-based-on-curly-brace-placement)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.4 Separate your statements properly

No matter if you use semicolons or not to separate your statements, knowing the common pitfalls of improper linebreaks or automatic semicolon insertion, will help you to eliminate regular syntax errors.

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Use ESLint to gain awareness about separation concerns. [Prettier](https://prettier.io/) or [Standardjs](https://standardjs.com/) can automatically resolve these issues.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** As seen in the previous section, JavaScript's interpreter automatically adds a semicolon at the end of a statement if there isn't one, or considers a statement as not ended where it should, which might lead to some undesired results. You can use assignments and avoid using immediately invoked ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô expressions to prevent most of the unexpected errors.

### Code example

```javascript
// Do
function doThing() {
    // ...
}

doThing()

// Do

const items = [1, 2, 3]
items.forEach(console.log)

// Avoid ‚Äî throws exception
const m = new Map()
const a = [1,2,3]
[...m.values()].forEach(console.log)
> [...m.values()].forEach(console.log)
>  ^^^
> SyntaxError: Unexpected token ...

// Avoid ‚Äî throws exception
const count = 2 // it tries to run 2(), but 2 is not a ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô
(function doSomething() {
  // do something amazing
}())
// put a semicolon before the immediate invoked ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô, after the const definition, save the return value of the anonymous ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô to a variable or avoid IIFEs altogether
```

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°:** "Semi ESLint rule"](https://eslint.org/docs/rules/semi)
üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°:** "No unexpected multiline ESLint rule"](https://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-unexpected-multiline)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.5 Name your ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Name all ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô, including closures and callbacks. Avoid anonymous ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô. This is especially useful when profiling a node app. Naming all ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô will allow you to easily understand what you're looking at when checking a memory snapshot

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** De‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Åging production issues using a core dump (memory snapshot) might become challenging as you notice significant memory consumption from anonymous ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.6 Use naming conventions for variables, constants, ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô and classes

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Use **_lowerCamelCase_** when naming constants, variables and ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô, **_UpperCamelCase_** (capital first letter as well) when naming classes and **_UPPER_SNAKE_CASE_** when naming global or static variables. This will help you to easily distinguish between plain variables, ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô, classes that require instantiation and variables declared at global module scope. Use descriptive names, but try to keep them short

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** JavaScript is the only language in the world that allows invoking a constructor ("Class") directly without instantiating it first. Consequently, Classes and ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô-constructors are differentiated by starting with UpperCamelCase

### 3.6 Code Example

```javascript
// for global variables names we use the const/let keyword and UPPER_SNAKE_CASE
let MUTABLE_GLOBAL = "mutable value"
const GLOBAL_CONSTANT = "immutable value";
const CONFIG = {
  key: "value",
};

// examples of UPPER_SNAKE_CASE convetion in nodejs/javascript ecosystem
// in javascript Math.PI module
const PI = 3.141592653589793;

// https://github.com/nodejs/node/blob/b9f36062d7b5c5039498e98d2f2c180dca2a7065/lib/internal/http2/core.js#L303
// in nodejs http2 module
const HTTP_STATUS_OK = 200;
const HTTP_STATUS_CREATED = 201;

// for class name we use UpperCamelCase
class SomeClassExample {
  // for static class properties we use UPPER_SNAKE_CASE
  static STATIC_PROPERTY = "value";
}

// for function names we use lowerCamelCase
function doSomething() {
  // for scoped variable names we use the const/let keyword and lowerCamelCase
  const someConstExample = "immutable value";
  let someMutableExample = "mutable value";
}
```

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.7 Prefer const over let. Ditch the var

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Using `const` means that once a variable is assigned, it cannot be reassigned. Preferring `const` will help you to not be tempted to use the same variable for different uses, and make your code clearer. If a variable needs to be reassigned, in a for loop, for example, use `let` to declare it. Another important aspect of `let` is that a variable declared using it is only available in the block scope in which it was defined. `var` is ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô scoped, not block-scoped, and [shouldn't be used in ES6](https://hackernoon.com/why-you-shouldnt-use-var-anymore-f109a58b9b70) now that you have `const` and `let` at your disposal

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** De‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Åging becomes way more cumbersome when following a variable that frequently changes

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: JavaScript ES6+: var, let, or const?** ](https://medium.com/javascript-scene/javascript-es6-var-let-or-const-ba58b8dcde75)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.8 Require modules first, not inside ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Require modules at the beginning of each file, before and outside of any ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô. This simple best practice will not only help you easily and quickly tell the dependencies of a file right at the top but also avoids a couple of potential problems

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Requires are run synchronously by Node.js. If they are called from within a ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô, it may block other requests from being handled at a more critical time. Also, if a required module or any of its dependencies throw an error and crash the server, it is best to find out about it as soon as possible, which might not be the case if that module is required from within a ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.9 Require modules by folders, as opposed to the files directly

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** When developing a module/library in a folder, place an index.js file that exposes the module's internals so every consumer will pass through it. This serves as an 'interface' to your module and eases future changes without breaking the contract

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Changing the internal structure of files or the signature may break the interface with clients

### 3.9 Code example

```javascript
// Do
module.exports.SMSProvider = require("./SMSProvider");
module.exports.SMSNumberResolver = require("./SMSNumberResolver");

// Avoid
module.exports.SMSProvider = require("./SMSProvider/SMSProvider.js");
module.exports.SMSNumberResolver = require("./SMSNumberResolver/SMSNumberResolver.js");
```

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.10 Use the `===` operator

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Prefer the strict equality operator `===` over the weaker abstract equality operator `==`. `==` will compare two variables after converting them to a common type. There is no type conversion in `===`, and both variables must be of the same type to be equal

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Unequal variables might return true when compared with the `==` operator

### 3.10 Code example

```javascript
"" == "0"; // false
0 == ""; // true
0 == "0"; // true

false == "false"; // false
false == "0"; // true

false == undefined; // false
false == null; // false
null == undefined; // true

" \t\r\n " == 0; // true
```

All statements above will return false if used with `===`

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.11 Use Async Await, avoid callbacks

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Node 8 LTS now has full support for Async-await. This is a new way of dealing with asynchronous code which supersedes callbacks and promises. Async-await is non-blocking, and it makes asynchronous code look synchronous. The best gift you can give to your code is using async-await which provides a much more compact and familiar code syntax like try-catch

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Handling async errors in callback style are probably the fastest way to hell - this style forces to check errors all over, deal with awkward code nesting, and makes it difficult to reason about the code flow

üîó[**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°:** Guide to async-await 1.0](https://github.com/yortus/asyncawait)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 3.12 Use arrow ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô expressions (=>)

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Though it's recommended to use async-await and avoid ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô parameters when dealing with older APIs that accept promises or callbacks - arrow ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô make the code structure more compact and keep the lexical context of the root ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô (i.e. `this`)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Longer code (in ES5 ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô) is more prone to ‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å and cumbersome to read

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: It‚Äôs Time to Embrace Arrow ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô**](https://medium.com/javascript-scene/familiarity-bias-is-holding-you-back-its-time-to-embrace-arrow-‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô-3d37e1a9bb75)

<br/><br/><br/>

<p align="right"><a href="#table-of-contents">‚¨Ü Return to top</a></p>

# `4. Testing And Overall Quality Practices`

## ![‚úî] 4.1 At the very least, write API (component) testing

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Most projects just don't have any automated testing due to short timetables or often the 'testing project' ran out of control and was abandoned. For that reason, prioritize and start with API testing which is the easiest way to write and provides more coverage than unit testing (you may even craft API tests without code using tools like [Postman](https://www.getpostman.com/)). Afterward, should you have more resources and time, continue with advanced test types like unit testing, DB testing, performance testing, etc

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** You may spend long days on writing unit tests to find out that you got only 20% system coverage

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.2 Include 3 parts in each test name

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Make the test speak at the requirements level so it's self-explanatory also to QA engineers and developers who are not familiar with the code internals. State in the test name what is being tested (unit under test), under what circumstances, and what is the expected result

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** A deployment just failed, a test named ‚ÄúAdd product‚Äù failed. Does this tell you what exactly is mal‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ôing?

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Include 3 parts in each test name**](./sections/testingandquality/3-parts-in-name.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.3 Structure tests by the AAA pattern

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Structure your tests with 3 well-separated sections: Arrange, Act & Assert (AAA). The first part includes the test setup, then the execution of the unit under test, and finally the assertion phase. Following this structure guarantees that the reader spends no brain CPU on understanding the test plan

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Not only you spend long daily hours on understanding the main code, but now also what should have been the simple part of the day (testing) stretches your brain

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Structure tests by the AAA pattern**](./sections/testingandquality/aaa.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.4 Detect code issues with a linter

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Use a code linter to check the basic quality and detect anti-patterns early. Run it before any test and add it as a pre-commit git-hook to minimize the time needed to review and correct any issue. Also check [Section 3](#3-code-style-practices) on Code Style Practices

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** You may let pass some anti-pattern and possible vulnerable code to your production environment.

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.5 Avoid global test fixtures and seeds, add data per-test

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** To prevent test coupling and easily reason about the test flow, each test should add and act on its own set of DB rows. Whenever a test needs to pull or assume the existence of some DB data - it must explicitly add that data and avoid mutating any other records

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Consider a scenario where deployment is aborted due to failing tests, team is now going to spend precious investigation time that ends in a sad conclusion: the system works well, the tests however interfere with each other and break the build

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Avoid global test fixtures**](./sections/testingandquality/avoid-global-test-fixture.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.6 Constantly inspect for vulnerable dependencies

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Even the most reputable dependencies such as Express have known vulnerabilities. This can get easily tamed using community and commercial tools such as üîó [npm audit](https://docs.npmjs.com/cli/audit) and üîó [snyk.io](https://snyk.io) that can be invoked from your CI on every build

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Keeping your code clean from vulnerabilities without dedicated tools will require to constantly follow online publications about new threats. Quite tedious

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.7 Tag your tests

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Different tests must run on different scenarios: quick smoke, IO-less, tests should run when a developer saves or commits a file, full end-to-end tests usually run when a new pull request is submitted, etc. This can be achieved by tagging tests with keywords like #cold #api #sanity so you can grep with your testing harness and invoke the desired subset. For example, this is how you would invoke only the sanity test group with [Mocha](https://mochajs.org/): mocha --grep 'sanity'

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Running all the tests, including tests that perform dozens of DB queries, any time a developer makes a small change can be extremely slow and keeps developers away from running tests

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.8 Check your test coverage, it helps to identify wrong test patterns

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Code coverage tools like [Istanbul](https://github.com/istanbuljs/istanbuljs)/[NYC](https://github.com/istanbuljs/nyc) are great for 3 reasons: it comes for free (no effort is required to benefit this reports), it helps to identify a decrease in testing coverage, and last but not least it highlights testing mismatches: by looking at colored code coverage reports you may notice, for example, code areas that are never tested like catch clauses (meaning that tests only invoke the happy paths and not how the app behaves on errors). Set it to fail builds if the coverage falls under a certain threshold

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** There won't be any automated metric telling you when a large portion of your code is not covered by testing

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.9 Inspect for outdated packages

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Use your preferred tool (e.g. `npm outdated` or [npm-check-updates](https://www.npmjs.com/package/npm-check-updates)) to detect installed outdated packages, inject this check into your CI pipeline and even make a build fail in a severe scenario. For example, a severe scenario might be when an installed package is 5 patch commits behind (e.g. local version is 1.3.1 and repository version is 1.3.8) or it is tagged as deprecated by its author - kill the build and prevent deploying this version

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Your production will run packages that have been explicitly tagged by their author as risky

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.10 Use production-like environment for e2e testing

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** End to end (e2e) testing which includes live data used to be the weakest link of the CI process as it depends on multiple heavy services like DB. Use an environment which is as close to your real production environment as possible like a-continue (Missed -continue here, needs content. Judging by the **‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá** clause, this should mention docker-compose)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Without docker-compose, teams must maintain a testing DB for each testing environment including developers' machines, keep all those DBs in sync so test results won't vary across environments

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.11 Refactor regularly using static analysis tools

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Using static analysis tools helps by giving objective ways to improve code quality and keeps your code maintainable. You can add static analysis tools to your CI build to fail when it finds code smells. Its main selling points over plain linting are the ability to inspect quality in the context of multiple files (e.g. detect duplications), perform advanced analysis (e.g. code complexity), and follow the history and progress of code issues. Two examples of tools you can use are [Sonarqube](https://www.sonarqube.org/) (2,600+ [stars](https://github.com/SonarSource/sonarqube)) and [Code Climate](https://codeclimate.com/) (1,500+ [stars](https://github.com/codeclimate/codeclimate)).

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** With poor code quality, ‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å and performance will always be an issue that no shiny new library or state of the art features can fix

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Refactoring!**](./sections/testingandquality/refactoring.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 4.12 Carefully choose your CI platform (Jenkins vs CircleCI vs Travis vs Rest of the world)

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Your continuous integration platform (CICD) will host all the quality tools (e.g. test, lint) so it should come with a vibrant ecosystem of plugins. [Jenkins](https://jenkins.io/) used to be the default for many projects as it has the biggest community along with a very powerful platform at the price of a complex setup that demands a steep learning curve. Nowadays, it has become much easier to set up a CI solution using SaaS tools like [CircleCI](https://circleci.com) and others. These tools allow crafting a flexible CI pipeline without the burden of managing the whole infrastructure. Eventually, it's a trade-off between robustness and speed - choose your side carefully

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Choosing some niche vendor might get you blocked once you need some advanced customization. On the other hand, going with Jenkins might burn precious time on infrastructure setup

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Choosing CI platform**](./sections/testingandquality/citools.md)

## ![‚úî] 4.13 Test your middlewares in isolation

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** When a middleware holds some immense logic that spans many requests, it is worth testing it in isolation without waking up the entire web framework. This can be easily achieved by stubbing and spying on the {req, res, next} objects

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** A ‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å in Express middleware === a ‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å in all or most requests

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Test middlewares in isolation**](./sections/testingandquality/test-middlewares.md)

<br/><br/><br/>

<p align="right"><a href="#table-of-contents">‚¨Ü Return to top</a></p>

# `5. Going To Production Practices`

## ![‚úî] 5.1. Monitoring

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Monitoring is a game of finding out issues before customers do ‚Äì obviously this should be assigned unprecedented importance. The market is overwhelmed with offers thus consider starting with defining the basic metrics you must follow (my suggestions inside), then go over additional fancy features and choose the solution that ticks all boxes. Click ‚ÄòThe Gist‚Äô below for an overview of the solutions

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Failure === disappointed customers. Simple

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Monitoring!**](./sections/production/monitoring.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.2. Increase transparency using smart logging

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Logs can be a dumb warehouse of de‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å statements or the enabler of a beautiful dashboard that tells the story of your app. Plan your logging platform from day 1: how logs are collected, stored and analyzed to ensure that the desired information (e.g. error rate, following an entire transaction through services and servers, etc) can really be extracted

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** You end up with a black box that is hard to reason about, then you start re-writing all logging statements to add additional information

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Increase transparency using smart logging**](./sections/production/smartlogging.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.3. Delegate anything possible (e.g. gzip, SSL) to a reverse proxy

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Node is awfully bad at doing CPU intensive tasks like gzipping, SSL termination, etc. You should use ‚Äòreal‚Äô middleware services like nginx, HAproxy or cloud vendor services instead

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Your poor single thread will stay busy doing infrastructural tasks instead of dealing with your application core and performance will degrade accordingly

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Delegate anything possible (e.g. gzip, SSL) to a reverse proxy**](./sections/production/delegatetoproxy.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.4. Lock dependencies

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Your code must be identical across all environments, but amazingly npm lets dependencies drift across environments by default ‚Äì when you install packages at various environments it tries to fetch packages‚Äô latest patch version. Overcome this by using npm config files, .npmrc, that tell each environment to save the exact (not the latest) version of each package. Alternatively, for finer grained control use `npm shrinkwrap`. \*Update: as of NPM5, dependencies are locked by default. The new package manager in town, Yarn, also got us covered by default

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** QA will thoroughly test the code and approve a version that will behave differently in production. Even worse, different servers in the same production cluster might run different code

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Lock dependencies**](./sections/production/lockdependencies.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.5. Guard process uptime using the right tool

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** The process must go on and get restarted upon failures. For simple scenarios, process management tools like PM2 might be enough but in today's ‚Äòdockerized‚Äô world, cluster management tools should be considered as well

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Running dozens of instances without a clear strategy and too many tools together (cluster management, docker, PM2) might lead to DevOps chaos

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Guard process uptime using the right tool**](./sections/production/guardprocess.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.6. Utilize all CPU cores

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** At its basic form, a Node app runs on a single CPU core while all others are left idling. It‚Äôs your duty to replicate the Node process and utilize all CPUs ‚Äì For small-medium apps you may use Node Cluster or PM2. For a larger app consider replicating the process using some Docker cluster (e.g. K8S, ECS) or deployment scripts that are based on Linux init system (e.g. systemd)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Your app will likely utilize only 25% of its available resources(!) or even less. Note that a typical server has 4 CPU cores or more, naive deployment of Node.js utilizes only 1 (even using PaaS services like AWS beanstalk!)

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Utilize all CPU cores**](./sections/production/utilizecpu.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.7. Create a ‚Äòmaintenance endpoint‚Äô

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Expose a set of system-related information, like memory usage and REPL, etc in a secured API. Although it‚Äôs highly recommended to rely on standard and battle-tested tools, some valuable information and operations are easier done using code

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** You‚Äôll find that you‚Äôre performing many ‚Äúdiagnostic deploys‚Äù ‚Äì shipping code to production only to extract some information for diagnostic purposes

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Create a ‚Äòmaintenance endpoint‚Äô**](./sections/production/createmaintenanceendpoint.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.8. Discover errors and downtime using APM products

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Application monitoring and performance products (a.k.a. APM) proactively gauge codebase and API so they can auto-magically go beyond traditional monitoring and measure the overall user-experience across services and tiers. For example, some APM products can highlight a transaction that loads too slow on the end-user's side while suggesting the root cause

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** You might spend great effort on measuring API performance and downtimes, probably you‚Äôll never be aware which is your slowest code parts under real-world scenario and how these affect the UX

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Discover errors and downtime using APM products**](./sections/production/apmproducts.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.9. Make your code production-ready

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Code with the end in mind, plan for production from day 1. This sounds a bit vague so I‚Äôve compiled a few development tips that are closely related to production maintenance (click Gist below)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** A world champion IT/DevOps guy won‚Äôt save a system that is badly written

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Make your code production-ready**](./sections/production/productioncode.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.10. Measure and guard the memory usage

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Node.js has controversial relationships with memory: the v8 engine has soft limits on memory usage (1.4GB) and there are known paths to leak memory in Node‚Äôs code ‚Äì thus watching Node‚Äôs process memory is a must. In small apps, you may gauge memory periodically using shell commands but in medium-large apps consider baking your memory watch into a robust monitoring system

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Your process memory might leak a hundred megabytes a day like how it happened at [Walmart](https://www.joyent.com/blog/walmart-node-js-memory-leak)

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Measure and guard the memory usage**](./sections/production/measurememory.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.11. Get your frontend assets out of Node

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Serve frontend content using dedicated middleware (nginx, S3, CDN) because Node performance really gets hurt when dealing with many static files due to its single-threaded model

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Your single Node thread will be busy streaming hundreds of html/images/angular/react files instead of allocating all its resources for the task it was born for ‚Äì serving dynamic content

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Get your frontend assets out of Node**](./sections/production/frontendout.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.12. Be stateless, kill your servers almost every day

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Store any type of data (e.g. user sessions, cache, uploaded files) within external data stores. Consider ‚Äòkilling‚Äô your servers periodically or use ‚Äòserverless‚Äô platform (e.g. AWS Lambda) that explicitly enforces a stateless behavior

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Failure at a given server will result in application downtime instead of just killing a faulty machine. Moreover, scaling-out elasticity will get more challenging due to the reliance on a specific server

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Be stateless, kill your Servers almost every day**](./sections/production/bestateless.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.13. Use tools that automatically detect vulnerabilities

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Even the most reputable dependencies such as Express have known vulnerabilities (from time to time) that can put a system at risk. This can be easily tamed using community and commercial tools that constantly check for vulnerabilities and warn (locally or at GitHub), some can even patch them immediately

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Keeping your code clean from vulnerabilities without dedicated tools will require you to constantly follow online publications about new threats. Quite tedious

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Use tools that automatically detect vulnerabilities**](./sections/production/detectvulnerabilities.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.14. Assign a transaction id to each log statement

Also known as correlation id / transit id / tracing id / request id / request context / etc.

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Assign the same identifier, transaction-id: {some value}, to each log entry within a single request. Then when inspecting errors in logs, easily conclude what happened before and after. Until version 14 of Node, this was not easy to achieve due to Node's async nature, but since AsyncLocalStorage came to town, this became possible and easy than ever. see code examples inside

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Looking at a production error log without the context ‚Äì what happened before ‚Äì makes it much harder and slower to reason about the issue

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Assign ‚ÄòTransactionId‚Äô to each log statement**](./sections/production/assigntransactionid.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.15. Set `NODE_ENV=production`

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Set the environment variable `NODE_ENV` to ‚Äòproduction‚Äô or ‚Äòdevelopment‚Äô to flag whether production optimizations should get activated ‚Äì many npm packages determine the current environment and optimize their code for production

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Omitting this simple property might greatly degrade performance. For example, when using Express for server-side rendering omitting `NODE_ENV` makes it slower by a factor of three!

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Set NODE_ENV=production**](./sections/production/setnodeenv.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.16. Design automated, atomic and zero-downtime deployments

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Research shows that teams who perform many deployments lower the probability of severe production issues. Fast and automated deployments that don‚Äôt require risky manual steps and service downtime significantly improve the deployment process. You should probably achieve this using Docker combined with CI tools as they became the industry standard for streamlined deployment

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Long deployments -> production downtime & human-related error -> team unconfident in making deployment -> fewer deployments and features

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.17. Use an LTS release of Node.js

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Ensure you are using an LTS version of Node.js to receive critical ‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å fixes, security updates and performance improvements

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Newly discovered ‡∏ö‡∏±‡πä‡∏Å or vulnerabilities could be used to exploit an application running in production, and your application may become unsupported by various modules and harder to maintain

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Use an LTS release of Node.js**](./sections/production/LTSrelease.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.18. Don't route logs within the app

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Log destinations should not be hard-coded by developers within the application code, but instead should be defined by the execution environment the application runs in. Developers should write logs to `stdout` using a logger utility and then let the execution environment (container, server, etc.) pipe the `stdout` stream to the appropriate destination (i.e. Splunk, Graylog, ElasticSearch, etc.).

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Application handling log routing === hard to scale, loss of logs, poor separation of concerns

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Log Routing**](./sections/production/logrouting.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 5.19. Install your packages with `npm ci`

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** You have to be sure that production code uses the exact version of the packages you have tested it with. Run `npm ci` to strictly do a clean install of your dependencies matching package.json and package-lock.json. Using this command is recommended in automated environments such as continuous integration pipelines.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** QA will thoroughly test the code and approve a version that will behave differently in production. Even worse, different servers in the same production cluster might run different code.

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Use npm ci**](./sections/production/installpackageswithnpmci.md)

<br/><br/><br/>

<p align="right"><a href="#table-of-contents">‚¨Ü Return to top</a></p>

# `6. Security Best Practices`

<div align="center">
<img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/OWASP%20Threats-Top%2010-green.svg" alt="54 items"/>
</div>

## ![‚úî] 6.1. Embrace linter security rules

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A1-Injection" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A1:Injection%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a> <a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A7-Cross-Site_Scripting_(XSS)" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20XSS%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Make use of security-related linter plugins such as [eslint-plugin-security](https://github.com/nodesecurity/eslint-plugin-security) to catch security vulnerabilities and issues as early as possible, preferably while they're being coded. This can help catching security weaknesses like using eval, invoking a child process or importing a module with a string literal (e.g. user input). Click '‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°' below to see code examples that will get caught by a security linter

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** What could have been a straightforward security weakness during development becomes a major issue in production. Also, the project may not follow consistent code security practices, leading to vulnerabilities being introduced, or sensitive secrets committed into remote repositories

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Lint rules**](./sections/security/lintrules.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.2. Limit concurrent requests using a middleware

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Denial_of_Service" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20DDOS%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** DOS attacks are very popular and relatively easy to conduct. Implement rate limiting using an external service such as cloud load balancers, cloud firewalls, nginx, [rate-limiter-flexible](https://www.npmjs.com/package/rate-limiter-flexible) package, or (for smaller and less critical apps) a rate-limiting middleware (e.g. [express-rate-limit](https://www.npmjs.com/package/express-rate-limit))

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** An application could be subject to an attack resulting in a denial of service where real users receive a degraded or unavailable service.

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Implement rate limiting**](./sections/security/limitrequests.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.3 Extract secrets from config files or use packages to encrypt them

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A6-Security_Misconfiguration" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A6:Security%20Misconfiguration%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a> <a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A3-Sensitive_Data_Exposure" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A3:Sensitive%20Data%20Exposure%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Never store plain-text secrets in configuration files or source code. Instead, make use of secret-management systems like Vault products, Kubernetes/Docker Secrets, or using environment variables. As a last resort, secrets stored in source control must be encrypted and managed (rolling keys, expiring, auditing, etc). Make use of pre-commit/push hooks to prevent committing secrets accidentally

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Source control, even for private repositories, can mistakenly be made public, at which point all secrets are exposed. Access to source control for an external party will inadvertently provide access to related systems (databases, apis, services, etc).

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Secret management**](./sections/security/secretmanagement.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.4. Prevent query injection vulnerabilities with ORM/ODM libraries

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A1-Injection" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A1:Injection%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** To prevent SQL/NoSQL injection and other malicious attacks, always make use of an ORM/ODM or a database library that escapes data or supports named or indexed parameterized queries, and takes care of validating user input for expected types. Never just use JavaScript template strings or string concatenation to inject values into queries as this opens your application to a wide spectrum of vulnerabilities. All the reputable Node.js data access libraries (e.g. [Sequelize](https://github.com/sequelize/sequelize), [Knex](https://github.com/tgriesser/knex), [mongoose](https://github.com/Automattic/mongoose)) have built-in protection against injection attacks.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Unvalidated or unsanitized user input could lead to operator injection when working with MongoDB for NoSQL, and not using a proper sanitization system or ORM will easily allow SQL injection attacks, creating a giant vulnerability.

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Query injection prevention using ORM/ODM libraries**](./sections/security/ormodmusage.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.5. Collection of generic security best practices

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** This is a collection of security advice that is not related directly to Node.js - the Node implementation is not much different than any other language. Click ‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏° to skim through.

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Common security best practices**](./sections/security/commonsecuritybestpractices.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.6. Adjust the HTTP response headers for enhanced security

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A6-Security_Misconfiguration" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A6:Security%20Misconfiguration%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Your application should be using secure headers to prevent attackers from using common attacks like cross-site scripting (XSS), clickjacking and other malicious attacks. These can be configured easily using modules like [helmet](https://www.npmjs.com/package/helmet).

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Attackers could perform direct attacks on your application's users, leading to huge security vulnerabilities

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Using secure headers in your application**](./sections/security/secureheaders.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.7. Constantly and automatically inspect for vulnerable dependencies

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A9-Using_Components_with_Known_Vulnerabilities" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A9:Known%20Vulnerabilities%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** With the npm ecosystem it is common to have many dependencies for a project. Dependencies should always be kept in check as new vulnerabilities are found. Use tools like [npm audit](https://docs.npmjs.com/cli/audit) or [snyk](https://snyk.io/) to track, monitor and patch vulnerable dependencies. Integrate these tools with your CI setup so you catch a vulnerable dependency before it makes it to production.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** An attacker could detect your web framework and attack all its known vulnerabilities.

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Dependency security**](./sections/security/dependencysecurity.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.8. Protect Users' Passwords/Secrets using bcrypt or scrypt

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A2-Broken_Authentication" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A9:Broken%20Authentication%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Passwords or secrets (e.g. API keys) should be stored using a secure hash + salt ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô like `bcrypt`,`scrypt`, or worst case `pbkdf2`.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Passwords and secrets that are stored without using a secure ‡∏ü‡∏±‡∏á‡∏Ñ‡πå‡∏ä‡∏±‡πà‡∏ô are vulnerable to brute forcing and dictionary attacks that will lead to their disclosure eventually.

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: User Passwords**](./sections/security/userpasswords.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.9. Escape HTML, JS and CSS output

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A7-Cross-Site_Scripting_(XSS)" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A7:XSS%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Untrusted data that is sent down to the browser might get executed instead of just being displayed, this is commonly referred as a cross-site-scripting (XSS) attack. Mitigate this by using dedicated libraries that explicitly mark the data as pure content that should never get executed (i.e. encoding, escaping)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** An attacker might store malicious JavaScript code in your DB which will then be sent as-is to the poor clients

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Escape output**](./sections/security/escape-output.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.10. Validate incoming JSON schemas

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A7-Cross-Site_Scripting_(XSS)" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A7: XSS%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a> <a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A8-Insecure_Deserialization" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A8:Insecured%20Deserialization%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** Validate the incoming requests' body payload and ensure it meets expectations, fail fast if it doesn't. To avoid tedious validation coding within each route you may use lightweight JSON-based validation schemas such as [jsonschema](https://www.npmjs.com/package/jsonschema) or [joi](https://www.npmjs.com/package/joi)

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Your generosity and permissive approach greatly increases the attack surface and encourages the attacker to try out many inputs until they find some combination to crash the application

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Validate incoming JSON schemas**](./sections/security/validation.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.11. Support blocklisting JWTs

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A2-Broken_Authentication" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A9:Broken%20Authentication%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** When using JSON Web Tokens (for example, with [Passport.js](https://github.com/jaredhanson/passport)), by default there's no mechanism to revoke access from issued tokens. Once you discover some malicious user activity, there's no way to stop them from accessing the system as long as they hold a valid token. Mitigate this by implementing a blocklist of untrusted tokens that are validated on each request.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Expired, or misplaced tokens could be used maliciously by a third party to access an application and impersonate the owner of the token.

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Blocklist JSON Web Tokens**](./sections/security/expirejwt.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.12. Prevent brute-force attacks against authorization

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A2-Broken_Authentication" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A9:Broken%20Authentication%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** A simple and powerful technique is to limit authorization attempts using two metrics:

1. The first is number of consecutive failed attempts by the same user unique ID/name and IP address.
2. The second is number of failed attempts from an IP address over some long period of time. For example, block an IP address if it makes 100 failed attempts in one day.

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** An attacker can issue unlimited automated password attempts to gain access to privileged accounts on an application

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Login rate limiting**](./sections/security/login-rate-limit.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.13. Run Node.js as non-root user

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A5-Broken_Access_Control" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A5:Broken%20Access%20Access%20Control-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** There is a common scenario where Node.js runs as a root user with unlimited permissions. For example, this is the default behaviour in Docker containers. It's recommended to create a non-root user and either bake it into the Docker image (examples given below) or run the process on this user's behalf by invoking the container with the flag "-u username"

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** An attacker who manages to run a script on the server gets unlimited power over the local machine (e.g. change iptable and re-route traffic to their server)

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Run Node.js as non-root user**](./sections/security/non-root-user.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.14. Limit payload size using a reverse-proxy or a middleware

<a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A8-Insecure_Deserialization" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20A8:Insecured%20Deserialization%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a> <a href="https://www.owasp.org/index.php/Top_10-2017_A1-Injection" target="_blank"><img src="https://img.shields.io/badge/%E2%9C%94%20OWASP%20Threats%20-%20DDOS%20-green.svg" alt=""/></a>

**‡∏¢‡∏≤‡∏ß‡πÑ‡∏õ‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô:** The bigger the body payload is, the harder your single thread works in processing it. This is an opportunity for attackers to bring servers to their knees without tremendous amount of requests (DOS/DDOS attacks). Mitigate this limiting the body size of incoming requests on the edge (e.g. firewall, ELB) or by configuring [express body parser](https://github.com/expressjs/body-parser) to accept only small-size payloads

**‡∏´‡∏£‡∏∑‡∏≠‡πÑ‡∏°‡πà‡∏Å‡πá:** Your application will have to deal with large requests, unable to process the other important work it has to accomplish, leading to performance implications and vulnerability towards DOS attacks

üîó [**‡∏≠‡πà‡∏≤‡∏ô‡πÄ‡∏û‡∏¥‡πà‡∏°‡πÄ‡∏ï‡∏¥‡∏°: Limit payload size**](./sections/security/requestpayloadsizelimit.md)

<br/><br/>

## ![‚úî] 6.15. Avoid JavaScript eval statements
